"},{"id":40390,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/jayson-tatum-boston-celtics-push-cleveland-cavaliers-brink-elimination","date":"2018-05-24","title":"The future is now: Boston Celtics rookie Jayson Tatum makes playoff history, pushes Cleveland Cavaliers to brink of elimination","content":"BOSTON \u2014 Someone might want to change their All-Rookie team ballot after this one. Jayson Tatum, so young that he actually drinks the Gatorade that\u2019s on the table when he has a podium game rather than leaving it there for cameras and branding, got 99 out of a 100 possible first-place votes from media folks for the newbie honors announced Tuesday. That left him a vote shy of both Philadelphia\u2019s Ben Simmons and Utah\u2019s Donovan Mitchell, the dueling favorites for the NBA\u2019s Rookie of the Year Award when it\u2019s announced next month. If Tatum merely is the Boston Celtics\u2019 favorite rookie, though, that\u2019s plenty. And wherever Simmons and Mitchell are at the moment, their seasons and postseasons are over. The Boston kid still is playing. Tatum scored 24 points, grabbed seven rebounds, dished four assists, pilfered four steals and blocked two shots to led the Celtics to their 96-83 Game 5 victory over the Cleveland Cavaliers Wednesday night at TD Garden. His plus\/minus rating of plus-19 was second only to veteran Al Horford\u2019s (plus-22) and in a pivotal game in which his teammates shot a combined 34 percent, Tatum \u2014 who turned 20 on March 3 \u2014 hit three of his seven 3-pointers, all but one of his eight free throws and seven of his 15 field-goal attempts overall. \u2022 Complete coverage of Eastern Conference finals \u201cI think his composure [is impressive], he plays above his age,\u201d LeBron James said earlier in the day. \u201cI think the unfortunate events of the injuries that they\u2019ve had have allowed him to, I believe, get better faster than I believe they expected here. It\u2019s given him an opportunity to make \u2026 make mistakes and learn from them and still be on the floor.\u201d Losing Gordon Hayward to a gruesome leg injury in the season\u2019s opening game and having Kyrie Irving limp into knee surgery and the sunset of this season in March did bump most of Boston\u2019s players, the rookie included, up a couple spots in coach Brad Stevens\u2019 pecking order. The No. 3 pick in last June\u2019s Draft, Tatum was going to get his share of playing time. But he wound up becoming the fifth rookie in NBA history, and the first since Stephen Curry in 2009-10, to score at least 1,000 points and hit at least 40 percent of his 3-pointers. Only eight previous rookies in Boston\u2019s storied franchise history totaled 1,000 or more points. Jaylen Brown, Boston\u2019s second-year wing, developed in tandem with Tatum. The pair of lithe, skilled players dripping with potential has most of the league\u2019s personnel execs and coaches drooling. Except, with Game 6 on Friday night in Cleveland for the first of two shots at eliminating the Cavaliers, the Celtics are playing as if their future is now. A truism in the NBA is that, by the end of a rookie\u2019s first arduous season, he\u2019s not a rookie anymore. Mix in some force-feeding due to Boston\u2019s two injured stars and now three playoff rounds, and Tatum is racing to the right on his learning curve. \u201cI think that we misuse the word \u2018development\u2019 sometimes,\u201d Stevens said. \u201cI think we\u2019re in the business of \u2018enhancement.\u2019 I think Jayson was ready to deal with everything that comes with this because of who he is and his family and all his coaches before, because he\u2019s a very emotionally steady, smart player that was going to perform at a high level above his age. \u201cI don\u2019t know that anybody could guess this as a rookie, but you knew he was going to be really good.\u201d Tatum sorta had to be in Game 5. Brown got matched up in a lot of Boston\u2019s defensive coverage of James and picked up his second and third personal fouls in the second quarter. Point guard Terry Rozier looked like his road alter ego, missing six of seven shots in the game\u2019s first 24 minutes. But Tatum \u2014 who averaged 12.7 points against Cleveland in three regular-season meetings but is at 17.2 so far in the East finals \u2014 had 12 points by halftime, helping the Celtics to their 53-42 lead. \u201cI just enjoy playing in the big moments, in the big games,\u201d Tatum said. \u201cI think that\u2019s when I have the most fun, when things are on the line.\u201d It was Tatum racing downcourt to chase down Kevin Love\u2019s errant pass into the backcourt and finish with a layup that had Boston up 74-58. And it was Tatum who drew a foul on Kyle Korver with 3:11 left, prompting Cavs coach Tyronn Lue to pull a weary James. \u201cI thought he was aggressive. I thought he was poised,\u201d Lue said of Tatum. \u201cEven though he was scoring the basketball, he didn\u2019t try to rush or he didn\u2019t press. \u2026 He played like a veteran.\u201d Tatum put in his work defensively Tuesday, but also got as good as he gave. It\u2019s become a familiar tactic for defenders to get physically aggressive with him, trying to exploit what at this stage still is limited strength by NBA standards. His father Justin, a basketball coach in St. Louis , has said he plays tall and hasn\u2019t yet learned to utilize his base. \u201cJR [Smith], Jeff Green, they\u2019re playing really hard on Tatum and making it very tough,\u201d Stevens said. \u201cHe\u2019s had a lot of experiences over the last couple weeks dealing with playoff defense. I thought Milwaukee guarded him exceptionally hard and were really committed when he drove to the rim to having multiple bodies there. I thought that Philly obviously guarded him very hard. It\u2019s hard to make plays at this level in these games, and he\u2019s done that pretty consistently.\u201d The numbers back that up. Tatum by halftime had become only the sixth rookie in league history to reach 300 points in the postseason, the first since Jack Sikma in 1978. It was his ninth playoff game of 20 points or more, tying him with Mitchell this season and David Robinson in 1990 for second most by a rookie since 1964; Kareem Abdul-Jabbar had 10 in 1970. Tatum, Brown and a few other young Celtics have given credit for the team\u2019s unexpected success \u2014 considering the injuries, anyway \u2014 to Al Horford, the most obvious grown-up in Boston\u2019s locker room. When Horford was asked late Tuesday what it\u2019s like for him being around \u201cthese kids,\u201d he sounded a little like James three years ago. That\u2019s when Irving was hobbling, eventually blowing out a knee that spring, and Kevin Love was done for the playoffs due to a shoulder injury suffered in the first round. That\u2019s also when James looked at the raw help he had from guys such as Tristan Thompson and Matthew Dellavedova, and locked in on the possibility of reaching the Finals. \u201cIt\u2019s a lot of fun, just because these guys, they want to play the right way,\u201d Horford said. \u201cThey play hard. I feel like we hold each other accountable out there. I think that\u2019s a big thing. And when those things happen, it becomes fun. It\u2019s fun to me. And there\u2019s no coincidence why we\u2019re in this position right now.\u201d Youth is being served, at least on the Celtics\u2019 floor. Steve Aschburner has written about the NBA since 1980. Last year, Milwaukee paid $2.3 million to settle a lawsuit over the death of Dontre Hamilton, a mentally ill black man fatally shot by a police officer after the officer roused him from a park bench downtown. Gobert was voted to the NBA All-Defensive First Team for the second year in a row, as selected by a global panel of 100 sportswriters and broadcasters. The 7-1 center from France earned 192 points, including 94 First Team votes. Davis, a two-time NBA All-Defensive Second Team selection, makes his debut on the First Team. The 6-11 forward\/center received the second-most points (163) and First Team votes (73), behind Gobert. The two big men are joined on the NBA All-Defensive First Team by Indiana Pacers guard Victor Oladipo (136 points), Pelicans guard Jrue Holiday (105) and Philadelphia 76ers forward Robert Covington (90). All three players are All-Defensive selections for the first time. The NBA All-Defensive Second Team consists of 76ers center Joel Embiid (90 points), Golden State Warriors forward Draymond Green (86), Boston Celtics forward\/center Al Horford (85), San Antonio Spurs guard Dejounte Murray (80) and Minnesota Timberwolves guard\/forward Jimmy Butler (79). Like the First Team, the Second Team has three first-time All-Defensive selections: Embiid, Horford and Murray. Embiid is the third finalist for the 2017-18 Kia NBA Defensive Player of the Year Award, joining Gobert and Davis. The winner will be announced at the 2018 NBA Awards presented by Kia on Monday, June 25 on TNT (9 p.m. ET). The second annual NBA Awards , honoring this season\u2019s top performers, will take place at Barker Hangar in Santa Monica, Calif. Players were awarded two points for each NBA All-Defensive First Team vote and one point for each Second Team vote. Voters selected two guards, two forwards and one center for each team, choosing players at the position they play regularly. Players who received votes at multiple positions were slotted at the position where they received the most votes. Complete voting results by media member will be posted at pr.nba.com the night of the NBA Awards presented by Kia .  Click here for the list of 100 media voters for the 2017-18 NBA All-Defensive Teams. 2017-18 NBA All-Defensive First Team Robert Covington, 76ers: The former NBA G League Rookie of the Year and All-Star Game MVP led the NBA in deflections and was tops in defensive win shares among players who appeared in at least 70 percent of their teams\u2019 games. The 76ers\u2019 defensive rating, which ranked third in the NBA, was 99.0 when Covington was on the court and 107.4 when he was off the court \u2013 a difference of 8.4 points per 100 possessions. Anthony Davis, Pelicans: A 2017-18 Kia NBA Most Valuable Player Award finalist, Davis led the NBA in blocked shots for the third time (2.57 bpg). He also finished fifth in the NBA in defending the rim (minimum 250 field goals defended), allowing opponents to shoot only 52.4 percent at the basket. Rudy Gobert, Jazz: Opponents shot 10.0 percentage points worse than expected on shots fewer than 6 feet from the basket against Gobert. Utah ranked second in the NBA in defensive rating by allowing 101.6 points per 100 possessions \u2013 a number that improved to 97.7 points per 100 possessions when Gobert was on the court. Jrue Holiday, Pelicans: New Orleans allowed 9.1 fewer points per 100 possessions with Holiday on the court than when he was off the court, the biggest difference for any Pelicans player. Victor Oladipo, Pacers: A 2017-18 Kia NBA Most Improved Player Award finalist, Oladipo averaged a league-leading 2.36 steals per game. 2017-18 NBA All-Defensive Second Team Jimmy Butler, Timberwolves: Butler averaged a career-high 1.97 steals per game, fourth best in the NBA.  Joel Embiid, 76ers: Opponents shot 7.8 percentage points worse than expected on all field goal attempts when Embiid was the closest defender, the NBA\u2019s best such mark (minimum 200 shots defended). Draymond Green, Warriors: The 2016-17 Kia NBA Defensive Player of the Year was one of four qualifying players to average at least 1.30 steals and 1.30 blocked shots per game. Al Horford, Celtics: An NBA All-Star for the fifth time, Horford helped Boston lead the NBA in defensive rating with 101.5 points allowed per 100 possessions. Dejounte Murray, Spurs: In his second season, Murray ranked second among point guards in defensive rebounding percentage (22.0), behind the Oklahoma City Thunder\u2019s Russell Westbrook (25.4). And finally: Durant, wobbly at the finish, dribbling up court with the game on the line \u2026 and shockingly surrendering the ball to Klay Thompson who was trapped deep in the corner, a poor decision leading to a poorly-aimed shot with a fraction of a second left. The Warriors have now played 31 postseason games since the signing of Durant in July 2016 made them the bully on the block, and their fourth-quarter Tuesday has its very own dubious place as the worst 12 minutes of this nearly two-year run. They were good for just 12 points on three buckets out of 18 attempts. They looked confused, panic-stricken, helpless and ultimately toast against the Rockets, losing 95-92 . And now the Western Conference finals are tied at two apiece after a pair of playoff beliefs were laid to rest: Golden State being unbeatable at home and nearly-unbeatable with Durant. They\u2019d won 16 straight at Oracle and were 29-4 overall with Durant (and undefeated at home with him). Perhaps a flat moment was inevitable, since nothing lasts forever, and the Rockets surely are no slouches, anyway. Still, it was jarring to witness the Warriors\u2019 inability to keep a comfortable lead and, once it vaporized, to snatch it back, something that comes naturally to champions. Also, not to single out one particular player \u2014 OK, well perhaps \u2014 but Durant was uncharacteristically timid in that fourth quarter, never taking control, never rescuing the Warriors the way Chris Paul saved the Rockets, delivering just one basket and then passing up a chance to be the hero at the finish. He seemed to be locked in a trance, unable to wake up or spring himself free. A bystander mostly. Ghost-like. That\u2019s just not in his DNA, which is why his stretch play in Game 4 was so weird. This was something new to Durant, the difference-maker last season during the Warriors\u2019 romp to a second title in three years, and someone who\u2019s playing at a consistently high level this spring. The screen shot of Game 4 is this: With 15 seconds left and the Rockets up two, James Harden missed a jumper, Green grabbed the rebound and gave it to Durant. With the clock ticking and the Rockets back pedaling, this was a stage made for Durant: Ball in his hands, with a chance to win or tie. Just the way the Warriors wanted it. Kerr didn\u2019t call a timeout in that situation, and debate that if you will; sometimes it\u2019s better to let the play develop, rather than allow the defense to set, and you also risk having to throw an inbounds pass. Besides, the Warriors had four veteran All-Stars on the floor. Do they really need a pointer or two? \u201cDraymond was trying to call one around four seconds and at that point the officials weren\u2019t looking,\u201d said Warriors coach Steve Kerr. \u201cBut I\u2019m always a proponent of pushing the ball off of a miss rather than call timeout. I thought we\u2019d get a better shot in transition. That\u2019s why I let them play.\u201d Durant crossed mid-court and the Rockets didn\u2019t immediately throw a double-team his way. Yet, the player who famously gut-punched LeBron James and the Cavaliers last summer with a pull-up three-pointer in a similar situation did not even look at the basket. He threw to Thompson, who appeared surprised, who was surrounded by Rockets and trapped in the extreme corner of the court, to the left of the basket, looking uncomfortable and unaccustomed to seeing the ball in his hands in this situation. Um, what? Of course, in hindsight, Durant would like a do-over. \u201cI was trying to see if I had some options,\u201d he said. \u201cI saw Klay running along the baseline and maybe I should\u2019ve waited until he set his feet. But I just threw a bounce pass. I wish it could\u2019ve been a better possession at the end. We\u2019ve got to live with that one.\u201d Or die with it, actually. \u201cI wish I had that play back,\u201d he admitted. \u201cI\u2019m going to watch film and see what my options were and hopefully if I\u2019m in that position again I\u2019ll be better.\u201d He yielded heavily to Curry, but the problem is Curry wasn\u2019t much better, making just a lone fourth-quarter basket himself and watching as the final shot of the game harmlessly nicked off the rim. Overall, the Warriors just didn\u2019t have it \u2014 they were \u201cfatigued\u201d to use Kerr\u2019s excuse \u2014 and lost a 12-point lead in the fourth and their command of the series as well. It went deeper than just a sloppy fourth. The Rockets were the tougher team both mentally and physically \u2014 Paul daring to go nostril to nostril with Draymond a handful of times \u2014 and simply battled. How many people figured the Rockets would fold after the Warriors dropped 34 on them in the third quarter, 17 from Curry, and flipped the score heavily in their favor? At that point, with the crowd roaring and sensing a quick series, and Curry splashing deep threes and doing shimmies again, and Durant with 21 points through three quarters, what could possibly go wrong for the home team? \u201cI mean, when you get a lead like that, it would help to sustain it,\u201d Curry said. The Warriors had only one assist in the fourth and their offensive sets were essentially a string of isolation plays. Again, that\u2019s not necessarily bad for them; Golden State thrives in any style. Yet the Rockets figured them out and the Warriors had no answer, mainly because the ball wouldn\u2019t fall. Sometimes, there are no other valid excuses; it\u2019s a make-or-miss league. They played without Andre Iguodala, resting with a bum knee. Iguodala often bails out the Warriors during rare tough stretches, yet the game was winnable even without him. Also, Thompson briefly left the game early with a knee issue yet returned and played without a limp. For the first time, a game in the West final had suspense after margins of 13, 22 and 41. The largest lead in the final nine minutes was only five. Basketball fans finally got what they wanted, a compelling game and now, perhaps, a series as well, since it\u2019s guaranteed to go at least six. What the Warriors want is some explanation from the Basketball Gods about what overcame them in the fourth quarter, because this was something new for Durant and crew. \u201cWe just ran out of gas,\u201d said Kerr. \u201cNot an ideal situation,\u201d said Curry. \u201cIt was there for the taking,\u201d said Thompson. They\u2019ll have two more games to reclaim their identity. Three if necessary. * * * Veteran NBA writer Shaun Powell has worked for newspapers and other publications for more than 25 years. "},{"id":40385,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/resilient-houston-rockets-rally-crucial-game-4","date":"2018-05-23","title":"Resilient Houston Rockets bite back, even series with epic Game 4 road win","content":"OAKLAND, Calif. \u2014 Maybe they are built for this after all, these rugged Houston Rockets. Twice they absorbed knockout blows from the reigning champion Golden State Warriors in a do-or-die Game 4 of the Western Conference finals in a raucous Oracle Arena. And both times the Rockets got up off the floor and battled back, showing championship mettle of their own, to do what no team has done to these Warriors since Kevin Durant joined them. The Rockets showed up five minutes late, battled back from a 12-0 blitz to start the game and a 27-8 third quarter avalanche to win 95-92 and tie this series at 2-2 and reclaim the home-court advantage they lost in Game 1. With the game, and their franchise-best 65-win regular season and basically everything on the line, the Rockets outplayed the mighty Warriors down the stretch to snap the NBA playoff-record 16-game home win streak. They proved that they belong on this big stage and that they are who they thought they were when they were dominating the league throughout the course of the regular season. \u201cI just think this was confidence,\u201d said veteran forward Trevor Ariza, the only player on the Rockets\u2019 roster who owns a championship ring (Los Angeles Lakers, 2009). \u201cWe\u2019re a confident team. We believe in ourselves and we went out and showed that we can win anywhere.\u201d It was the Warriors, the group with all of the experience in these moments, that melted down late in the game, not the Rockets. The pressure that Rockets coach Mike D\u2019Antoni insisted was on the Warriors after his team\u2019s 41-point loss in Game 3 Sunday was there. The Rockets outscored the Warriors 25-12 in the fourth quarter. The Warriors shot just 3-for-18 after torching the Rockets for 34 points, 17 from Stephen Curry, in a third quarter that looked like one of their signature waves that usually slams the door on the opposition. But not this time. Not with the Rockets playing their best defensive quarter of the season, according to D\u2019Antoni. \u201cYeah, I thought it was the highest level we\u2019ve ever played defensively, without a doubt,\u201d he said. \u201cBecause you\u2019re talking about maybe the best offensive team ever, and they got on a roll. Even when we were down 12-zip, there was some good defense in there to get us back, because we weren\u2019t lighting it up to get it back. \u201cSo (we) just got a lot of tough stops and a lot of tough rebounds, getting loose balls and we didn\u2019t get into foul trouble too early. It was just a lot of good things. Great switching and they got a little tired in the fourth quarter, and that\u2019s because they felt us for three quarters. If we can repeat that, and that\u2019s what the formula is, and we\u2019ll see if we can do that when we get to Houston.\u201d The Rockets couldn\u2019t have gone home even without the work Chris Paul put in during the first pressure-cooker game of this series. Playing on a sore foot, he was nothing short of magnificent in the fourth, scoring eight of his 27 points, while showing the sort of toughness the Rockets lacked before his arrival last summer in a blockbuster trade. \u201cMan, he\u2019s been doing it for so long,\u201d James Harden said of his fellow superstar point guard. \u201cNow he has an opportunity to do it on this stage. I mean, everybody knows how great he is, from his passing ability to his big shot-making ability, and even to his defense. He was huge for us tonight.\u201d That\u2019s all Paul was focused on. One game. One night. One chance to make things right. \u201cIt was a good win for us,\u201d he said. \u201cWe knew we needed it, but we said all along with both teams home court doesn\u2019t really matter. Both teams have the ability to win on the road. We had to prove that to ourselves. Weathering the storm, the runs that they made, and knowing that now we got a chance to go back home, we knew we had to get at least one win here. We got it, so now it\u2019s a three-game series.\u201d D\u2019Antoni only used seven players to get the job done, leaning on his core group in a grueling game to flip this series into a best-of-three with the Rockets back in a position of power. The trust and faith he showed in his core group paid off. \u201c We \u2019 re confident in what we do, \u201d  Ariza said.  \u201c When we are locked in to what we are doing and what we are supposed to be doing, we are a really good defensive team. We \u2019 re a really good team, period. We just came out and played hard tonight. For all the hard-earned hype about the Warriors and what they are capable of, the Rockets still haven\u2019t lost consecutive games in this postseason. They are 4-2 on the road, 2-0 in games decided by three points or less and a perfect 5-0 when Paul scores 25 or more points. They still have work to do in this series, of course, but they are on a path that suggests they possess the sort of fiber needed to make it into the championship discussion. D\u2019Antoni called them soft after that Game 3 embarrassment. He praised their toughness on this night, and rightfully so. \u201cWe\u2019ve been doing it all year long,\u201d said Harden, who scored just two of his game-high 30 points in the fourth quarter. \u201cThat\u2019s the main reason we\u2019re in the position we\u2019re in today. That third game was just one loss. We all know that. We\u2019ve got the mentality that we\u2019re going to win Game 4. We talked about it. We\u2019ve preached it. \u201cThey made runs and they were going to, especially at home. And we kept fighting, kept fighting and defensively kept locking in and making big-time shots. Chris and Eric (Gordon) and Trevor, guys made big-time shots in that fourth quarter.\u201d A fourth quarter that changed this series and could potentially change the entire postseason landscape, depending on what comes next from this team with its destiny back in its own hands. The First Team also features Los Angeles Lakers forward Kyle Kuzma (93 First Team votes) and Chicago Bulls forward Lauri Markkanen (76). Mitchell, Simmons and Tatum are the three finalists for the 2017-18 Kia NBA Rookie of the Year award. The second annual NBA Awards , honoring this season\u2019s top performers, will take place at Barker Hangar in Santa Monica, Calif. He joined Kobe Bryant (2007-08) as the only Lakers players to reach those marks. Donovan Mitchell, Jazz (20.5 ppg\/3.7 rpg\/3.7 apg\/1.49 spg): Mitchell became the first rookie to lead a 45-plus-win team (48-34) in scoring since the San Antonio Spurs\u2019 David Robinson in 1989-90. The four-time Kia NBA Western Conference Rookie of the Month set the NBA rookie record for three-pointers made with 187. Ben Simmons, 76ers (15.8 ppg\/8.2 apg\/8.1 rpg\/1.73 spg): Simmons joined Oscar Robertson (1960-61) as the only rookies in NBA history to average at least 15.0 points, 8.0 assists and 8.0 rebounds per game. A four-time Kia NBA Eastern Conference Rookie of the Month, the Australian native led rookies in rebounding, assists and steals average while helping the 76ers (52-30) finish with the third-best record in the East. Jayson Tatum, Celtics (13.9 ppg\/5.0 rpg\/47.5 FG%\/43.4 3FG%): Tatum led rookies and ranked eighth among all NBA players in three-point field goal percentage. The Kia NBA Eastern Conference Rookie of the Month for December started in all 80 of his appearances for the No. 2 team in the East (55-27). 2017-18 NBA All-Rookie Second Team Lonzo Ball, Lakers (10.2 ppg\/7.2 apg\/6.9 rpg\/1.69 spg): Ball ranked second among rookies in assists and steals average and fourth in rebounding average while playing a rookie-leading 34.2 minutes per game. Bogdan Bogdanovic, Kings (11.8 ppg\/3.3 apg\/44.6 FG%\/39.2 3FG%): The Serbian guard was the fourth-leading rookie in both three-point field goal percentage and three-pointers made (129). John Collins, Hawks (10.5 ppg\/7.3 rpg\/1.08 bpg\/57.6 FG%): Collins set a franchise rookie record for field goal percentage and became the sixth rookie in Hawks history to average at least 10.0 points and 7.0 rebounds. Josh Jackson, Suns (13.1 ppg\/4.6 rpg\/1.04 spg\/25.4 mpg): Jackson averaged 18.5 points and 6.1 rebounds in his final 29 games of the season, and he scored at least 15 points in each of his last 12 games. Dennis Smith Jr., Mavericks (15.2 ppg\/5.2 apg\/3.8 rpg\/1.03 spg): Smith, the first Dallas rookie to post a triple-double since Jason Kidd (1994-95), tied for fourth among rookies in scoring average and was third in assists average. And while basketball is a team game, this one came down to an old-fashioned shootout between Atlanta\u2019s Dominique Wilkins and Boston\u2019s Larry Bird. \u201cIt was like two gunfighters waiting to blink,\u201d recalled Celtics forward Kevin McHale. \u201cThere was one stretch that was as pure a form of basketball as you\u2019re ever going to see.\u201d The game was tied 86-86 with 10:26 to play when the teams\u2019 respective stars took over. \u201cThey each put their team on their back and said, \u2018Let\u2019s go,'\u201d said Hawks coach Mike Fratello. * Legends Profile: Larry Bird Bird fired the first shot, a jumper with 10:03 to play, and went on to score nine points in a span of 1:58. But Atlanta stayed close and drew even again at 99-99 on a basket by Wilkins with 5:57 left. Bird scored 11 points after that, including the go-ahead basket with 3:34 to play and a stunning three-pointer over Wilkins with 1:43 left. Wilkins matched Bird\u2019s 11 points during that stretch, but it was not enough. With his team down by two points with one second left, Wilkins intentionally missed the second of two free throws, but Boston\u2019s Robert Parish tipped the rebound to teammate Dennis Johnson as the buzzer sounded and the Celtics had a 118-116 victory. * Legends Profile: Dominique Wilkins Wilkins ended up with a game-high 47 points, shooting a brilliant 19-for-23 from the floor. But it was the Celtics who were left standing at the end thanks to Bird, who finished with 34 points on 15-for-24 from the field, 20 of those points coming in the fourth quarter. \u201cHe wanted it,\u201d said Don Chaney, an assistant coach with the Hawks at the time but a former teammate of Bird\u2019s. \u201cHe wanted the ball and he came through. The Sager Strong Award, named for iconic Turner Sports sideline reporter Craig Sager, is presented annually to an individual who has been a trailblazer while exemplifying courage, faith, compassion and grace. The award is bestowed upon the recipient in the form of a colorful suit jacket, a replica of the one worn by Sager during his unforgettable \u201cTime is simply how you live your life\u201d speech in 2016. One of basketball\u2019s most respected defensive players and rebounders, Mutombo is also well regarded beyond the game for his humanitarian work around the world. Two decades ago he created the Dikembe Mutombo Foundation, dedicated to improving the health, education and quality of life for the people of his native Democratic Republic of the Congo. Among the many achievements for DMF, the organization opened the Biamba Marie Mutombo Hospital in 2007, and since, the facility has treated nearly a quarter million patients. In 2009, Mutombo was named a global ambassador for the NBA by NBA Commissioner Emeritus David Stern. The basketball Hall of Famer originally came to the United States in 1987 on an academic scholarship to Georgetown. Later, the school\u2019s legendary coach John Thompson invited him to try out for the basketball team. Eventually, he would be a first round NBA Draft pick in 1991, and go on to play 19 years in the NBA before retiring in 2009. The 2018 NBA Awards on TNT \u2013 presented live from historic Barker Hangar in Los Angeles \u2013 will honor all of the league\u2019s top performers from the 2017-18 NBA season, including the exclusive unveiling of the Kia NBA MVP, Kia NBA Defensive Player of the Year, Kia NBA Rookie of the Year and Lifetime Achievement Award, among others. The second annual NBA Awards on TNT will once again feature current and former NBA players, coaches, musical performances and celebrity presenters throughout the evening. Additionally, the Sports Emmy Award-winning Inside the NBA studio team of Ernie Johnson, Charles Barkley, Kenny Smith and Shaquille O\u2019Neal will be integrated throughout the show. Additional details will be announced at a later date. Last year\u2019s first-ever Sager Strong recipient was Monty Williams, who has spent more than two decades as a player, coach and executive with the Portland Trail Blazers, New Orleans Hornets\/Pelicans (as head coach), Oklahoma City Thunder and San Antonio Spurs. His legacy throughout the basketball community extends beyond the court, as someone who has repeatedly faced adversity while remaining a beacon of compassion, loyalty, faith and family."},{"id":46691,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/nba-soundsystem-houston-culture-hip-hop","date":"2018-05-22","title":"Sounds of Houston with Rice University professor Dr. Anthony Pinn","content":"Rice University professor Dr. Anthony Pinn, who teaches a class on religion and hip-hop culture, joins the show to talk about his studies, the history of Houston music and how it all intersects with the basketball world. * * * Be sure to subscribe on Apple Podcasts or iHeart Radio  for more NBA Soundsystem all season long. It can play hard, it can play together, and it can play smart. The Boston Celtics played harder and more together in Game 4 of the Eastern Conference finals than they did two nights earlier, when they lost to the Cleveland Cavaliers by 30 points. \u201cWe responded,\u201d Jaylen Brown said afterward. \u201cIt was a better game and a better effort by our team.\u201d The Celtics played hard and played together. Two out of three ain\u2019t bad, but two out of three isn\u2019t enough on the road against a team led by LeBron James. The Celtics didn\u2019t play very smart on Monday, and a 111-102 victory for the Cavs has this series tied at two games apiece. Really, the first 24 minutes of Game 4 was one of the dumber halves of basketball you will ever see from a team that had been putting on a clinic of execution over an eight-game stretch from Game 7 of the first round through Game 2 of the conference finals. In the first quarter, Brown pushed the ball up the floor after a Cleveland bucket, only to have Marcus Smart \u2013 29 percent from 3-point range in his career \u2013 shoot a 3 (his second missed jumper in as many possessions) with 19 seconds on the shot clock. Shortly thereafter, with the Cavs in the bonus, the Celtics committed three straight fouls more than 15 feet from the basket, sending Cleveland to the line for free points. And with the shot clock off at the end of the first, Brown tried to score too early and missed a dunk, giving the Cavs another chance to build on what was already a 16-point lead. In the first six minutes of the second quarter, the Celtics fouled the Cavs three times on jump shots. Late in the second, Smart rebounded a George Hill miss and, as he was falling out of bounds, tossed the ball behind his back \u2026 right to Hill for an easy layup. And on the ensuing Celtics possession, Semi Ojeleye, who has made five pull-up 3-pointers this season, attempted one with 10 seconds left to shoot. It seemed that no Celtic was immune to being boneheaded. Brown said that they were \u201cjust going too fast, too excited.\u201d \u201cWe need to slow down,\u201d he said. \u201cWe missed a bunch of easy opportunities. We made some bad turnovers and things like that.\u201d The second half was better, but the Celtics never aggressively attacked Kevin Love after he picked up his fifth foul early in the third quarter (and returned to start the fourth). Marcus Morris made sure that Smart wasn\u2019t the only guy who saved the ball under the opponent\u2019s basket, gifting James with a layup after initially intercepting his pass during a crucial stretch. And when the Celtics had chances to make it a two-possession game in the fourth, they took just a few too many bad shots. \u201cI think obviously we\u2019ve got to play better than we did,\u201d Celtics coach Brad Stevens said when asked about mental mistakes. \u201cI\u2019ll go through film and we\u2019ll re-look at it and determine the main reasons why we were where we were, but certainly we didn\u2019t play a perfect game.\u201d So the series is tied 2-2 and with the way things have gone, it has become more difficult for Stevens to downplay the home-road narrative that he\u2019d like to keep from seeping into his locker room. While the coach has said that he wasn\u2019t \u201closing sleep over where we\u2019re playing right now,\u201d his team clearly hasn\u2019t played like it\u2019s been oblivious of the environment. To Stevens\u2019 point, the game should be the same, whether you\u2019re playing at home or on the road. The result should be about how the players play, not the color of the floor or the support of the crowd. But that simply hasn\u2019t been the case in these playoffs for the Celtics, who are 9-0 at TD Garden and now 1-6 on the road. \u201cIt\u2019s much harder,\u201d Al Horford admitted. \u201cWe have to be better. We have to execute better. We have to do all those things in order to win. It\u2019s hard to win on the road, as we found out here.\u201d Over the last five years, home-court advantage has been worth less than three points per game in the regular season and a little more than four points per game in the playoffs. This year, the Celtics ranked third with 28 regular-season wins on the road. But in the playoffs, the difference between the Celtics at home (plus-11.3) and on the road (minus-12.0) has been more than 23 points per game. Their only road win (Game 3 of the conference semifinals in Philadelphia) came in overtime. In the conference finals, the Celtics are a plus-38 in Boston and a minus-39 in Cleveland. They haven\u2019t been totally \u201crattled\u201d at Quicken Loans Arena, but they\u2019ve been rushed, uncomfortable, and undisciplined. And because of that, the Celtics will be coming back to Cleveland for Game 6. They don\u2019t need to win here to win the series, but given how they\u2019ve played in Cleveland so far, they need to stay undefeated at home. John Schuhmann is a staff writer for NBA.com. That\u2019s when LeBron James and Kevin Love, handling their postgame interview duties in tandem, were asked to explain all the extra passes, the defenders flying around, and the energy and effort that was so apparent, compared to the first two games. Why, in other words, was such hustle and winning plays at the ready some nights and so conspicuously absent on others? \u201cI don\u2019t know,\u201d James said, his face in shadow from the bill of his cap. \u201cI don\u2019t know, either,\u201d Love said, a beat or two later. Kyle Korver took more of a crack at it after Cleveland repeated the performance Monday, fending off the Boston Celtics in Game 4 to even the best-of-seven series at two games apiece. This time it was closer, a 111-102 Cavaliers victory rather than the 30-point blowout two nights earlier. But that only accentuated the intangibles, the grimy work the Cavs did better than the Celtics possession after possession. Cleveland could point afterward to various miscues and breakdowns that prevented it from building the lead Monday to the breezy levels of Game 3. Then again, the Cavaliers managed their advantage adeptly, fending off a Boston team that reclaimed some of its feistiness in the second half. No matter what sort of run the Celtics made in the third and fourth quarters, the Cavs kept them three possessions behind. That\u2019s as close as Boston got, and no closer. Not that Korver was any better at explaining why this time and why not those other times. \u201cI\u2019m not going to give you a great answer either, because you\u2019re supposed to do it all the time,\u201d the veteran shooter said. \u201cYou want to have that mentality all the time. \u201cSometimes you don\u2019t always get opportunities like that in a game. I had a loose ball in the first half that I didn\u2019t dive on, and I was mad at myself afterwards. I was in the mindset tonight of doing that, but I didn\u2019t do it on that one.\u201d There\u2019d be no second regret. If there was one play that typified Cleveland\u2019s success in shortening the East finals now to best-of-three, resuming on the Celtics\u2019 floor at TD Garden Wednesday ( 8:30 p.m. ET, ESPN ), it was Korver diving headlong after a loose ball near the end of the third quarter. Cleveland point guard George Hill tied up Boston big man Aron Baynes for a jump ball mismatch, so James and Korver flashed some quick communication that they intended to steal Baynes\u2019 inevitable tap. \u201cThey were tipping it back and \u2018Bron saw me going,\u201d Korver explained. \u201cI was going, but I wasn\u2019t going that far. And he hit it all the way (downcourt). So I just took off after it. And I felt Terry (Rozier) run right past me. I was like, \u2018Oh, I\u2019ve got to dive after this thing.\u2019\u201d Korver did dive, and had a bead on the ball. Rozier was at a disadvantage, trying to locate it on the fly, and the result when the ball squirted out of bounds proved it: Cavaliers basketball. \u201cI felt so incredibly old and slow when I dove after that ball,\u201d Korver said. \u201cBut the heart was in the right spot.\u201d At 37, Korver had the sort of gritty game that propels good teams through the postseason. He scored 14 points on 4-of-7 shooting in his 25 minutes, winding up as the game\u2019s most prolific bench scorer. But the 6-foot-7 marksman, usually offered faint praise as a \u201csolid team defender,\u201d also blocked three shots, getting his hands on the ball to disrupt Boston possessions and generally tormented Jaylen Brown when they were matched up. Brown shot 4-of-14 for just 10 points through the first three quarters. \u201cHe\u2019s guarding \u2014 how old is Jaylen Brown?\u201d James asked. \u201cTwenty-one? He\u2019s guarding Jaylen Brown, one of the most athletic wings we have in our league. Jaylen can fall on the ground 10 times and probably spring up and just as likely never feel it. I don\u2019t remember Kyle falling too much like that. \u201cBut listen, he\u2019s doing whatever it takes to try to help us win, with the blocks, with the strips. Obviously his shot-making is very key for our team as well, but it\u2019s just the intangibles he\u2019s doing for us defensively that has put him in a position to be on the floor.\u201d Said Cavs coach Tyronn Lue after being reminded that Korver \u2013 drafted in the same 2003 Draft as James, only 50 picks later after four years at Creighton \u2013 has been 37 since St. Patrick\u2019s Day: \u201cGod dang. We\u2019re playing him too many minutes.\u201d There were multiple Cavaliers flying around defensively, to use their vernacular, and chipping in small moments and prized intangibles. They needed them all, too, on a night when they weren\u2019t all that sharp handling the ball (19 turnovers worth 19 points to Boston) or shooting it from distance (8-for-23, compared to 17-of-34 in Game 3). So they needed the work of center Tristan Thompson, who has made Boston\u2019s Al Horford battle for everything since Lue flipped Thompson into the starting lineup in Game 2. Thompson scored 13 points with 12 rebounds and a pair of blocks. Then there was Larry Nance Jr., bouncy and pesky, scoring seven points in 10-plus minutes with a pair of blocks and a couple of offensive rebounds. James had the night\u2019s gaudiest number, scoring 44 points in 42 minutes. But even then, it was James\u2019 repeated exploitation of Rozier as a switched and generally overmatched defender, along with finishes at the rim and \u201chockey assists\u201d to initiate plays that kept Cleveland in front. Now all the Cavaliers need to do is replicate the performance in Boston. The series could be decided entirely according to home court, but both the Celtics and the Cavaliers are frantic to win at least one on their opponents\u2019 floor. The former could make their task a little easier by doing so, the latter can\u2019t advance if they don\u2019t snag either Game 5 or Game 7. \u201cHave the same approach going into Boston,\u201d Lue described his message to the players. \u201cI think playing with more speed and more pace, pushing the basketball. I think taking care of the basketball is the most important, especially on the road. You don\u2019t want to turn the ball over when you get to Boston because they really thrive off that \u2014 dunks, 3s, layups.\u201d Nothing can match the satisfaction a sniper like Korver feels when he nails several soul-crushing, quick-release 3-pointers against scrambling defenders. But beating the other guy to a floor burn has its rewards, too. \u201cIt\u2019s hard to get here,\u201d Korver said of the conference championship series, one step shy of The Finals. \u201cJust because LeBron\u2019s been here so many years in a row, sometimes some people can take it for granted and just expect it to happen. It\u2019s hard to get this far in the playoffs. It\u2019s hard to win a playoff series. \u201cYou\u2019ve got to have the opportunity and you\u2019ve just got to be ready for it. Maybe some guys don\u2019t like doing those plays. But in the playoffs, you should be going after all of them.\u201d Steve Aschburner has written about the NBA since 1980. Budenholzer was named the NBA coach of the year in 2015, when he led the Hawks to a franchise-record 60 wins and an appearance in the Eastern Conference finals. The Hawks held foes to 97.1 points per game and 36 percent shooting that season. Atlanta went an Eastern Conference-worst 24-58 this season. But they were rarely blown out, losing 21 games by fewer than 10 points and only seven by 20 or more points. Atlanta is rebuilding. Budenholzer now takes over a team moving into a new downtown arena that is in position to challenge for a top-four seed in the East next year \u2013 especially if it can play more consistent defense. \u201cI think with the individual talents we have in Milwaukee \u2026 I think one of the words I used in the interview process was, `How can we unlock this talent defensively?\u201d\u2018 Budenholzer said. \u201cI just think there\u2019s so much to work with.\u201d Start with the 6-foot-11 Antetokounmpo, whose length and athleticism make him a threat on both ends of the floor. Khris Middleton has grown into a good two-way player, while Eric Bledsoe and Malcolm Brogdon provide toughness at point guard. The Bucks are coming off a 44-win season and third playoff appearance in four years. They also allowed 106.8 points a game and had problems with rebounding and defending the 3-point line, and coach Jason Kidd was fired at midseason. In Budenholzer, they got an experienced coach with a track record of developing players and a resume that traces back to a 17-year stint as an assistant with the San Antonio Spurs. San Antonio won four NBA titles while Budenholzer was there. \u201cFinding the right person, the right fit for this team \u2026 to help this group take the next step was paramount,\u201d general manager Jon Horst said. \u201cUltimately after going through the process, it was clear that Bud was the right guy to do that.\u201d Budenholzer said players would be able to understand his defensive principles quickly, which would help in \u201cfreeing them up to be great on that side of the court.\u201d The details are still being worked out. He\u2019s barely been on the job for five days, and he\u2019s hoping that most of his staff from Atlanta follows him to Milwaukee. Budenholzer hasn\u2019t even met the whole team. But he has had breakfast already with the Bucks\u2019 two best players, Middleton and Antetokounmpo. Building a solid relationship with Antetokounmpo, especially, might be his one of his most important tasks for now. \u201cAnd those conversations, I look forward to having with Giannis and listening to Giannis too. He\u2019s a smart player,\u201d Budenholzer said. \u201cI think together, he and I will probably push each other. But I look forward to pushing him. He believes it, I believe it. The bruise reportedly is slightly below Iguodala\u2019s left knee cap."},{"id":40429,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/morning-tip-nba-prepares-sports-betting","date":"2018-05-21","title":"In wake of Supreme Court ruling, NBA preparing for impact of sports betting","content":"But the woman took off the great lid of the jar with her hands and scattered all these and her thought caused sorrow and mischief to men. Only Hope remained there in an unbreakable home within under the rim of the great jar and did not fly out at the door; for ere that, the lid of the jar stopped her, by the will of Aegis-holding Zeus who gathers the clouds. But the rest, countless plagues, wander amongst men; for earth is full of evils and the sea is full. \u2013Hesiod, Works and Days The fable of what became known as Pandora\u2019s Box, rather than Pandora\u2019s Jar (the original wording, per Hesiod, having changed in translation over the centuries), resonates more than ever today, in a world in which we want immediate answers before we even know what the right questions are to ask. The notion of unintended consequences is front and center as we learn more and more rapidly because of technology but spend less and less time contemplating what we\u2019ve learned\u2014also, in large part, because of technology. The Supreme Court\u2019s 6-3 decision last week that opened the door to legalizing gambling on sports in the United States will do a few things we already know. It will inject hundreds of millions of dollars into state coffers around the country, as legislatures and municipalities rapidly approve bills that will allow residents of their respective states to bet on, basically, anything\u2014but, from now on, legally, with the states getting the lion\u2019s share of the revenues. The ruling will allow states to legally set up sports books, which will allow citizens of those states to make bets on games without having to drive to Las Vegas or call a 900 number on some island in the Atlantic. Nineteen states, led by New Jersey\u2014which set all this in motion when its citizens passed a nonbinding referendum in 2012 legalizing sports betting, and whose state legislature soon after codified that referendum into state law\u2014had fought the federal government in court the last five years, and had lost almost every decision in the courts until last week. Those and other states are now scrambling to get sports books and casinos up and running as soon as possible. \u201cThis is their new lottery ticket,\u201d said Michele Roberts, the Executive Director of the National Basketball Players Association, in a phone interview Saturday. The SCOTUS decision, striking down the Professional and Amateur Sports Protection Act (PASPA), enacted in 1992, will create a tsunami of interest in sports across the board going forward\u2014collegiate and pro. Hardcore fans will now be able to put a bet on whether the next pitch will be a ball or a strike; whether the field goal will go wide left, wide right or down the middle; if the 50 percent foul shooter makes the next one or not. But, as is the case with March Madness and the NCAA Tournament, people in every office, car pool, dorm or church will be able to participate as well. Casual fans who don\u2019t follow every drop of the puck or grind through 162 regular season baseball games will nonetheless tune in on their various devices to see the outcomes of innings, quarters, halves and periods. We know that sports leagues and their television partners will, one way or another, be further enriched, with the attention already paid to their games and broadcasts almost certain to grow exponentially as more people place legal bets on the various outcomes. And more eyeballs viewing\/consuming mean bigger ratings, more clicks and more advertising dollars. And, we know Las Vegas, no matter which other municipalities get up to speed in the coming years, is going to remain front and center in setting the lines and odds and everything else that develops. \u201cWe\u2019ve been preparing for this decision for quite some time now,\u201d said Jay Kornegay, the vice president of Race and Sports SuperBook at the Westgate Las Vegas Resort and Casino, the largest of its kind in the state. \u201cWe\u2019re not of the position that considered (the decision) a threat,\u201d Kornegay said. \u201cWe\u2019re in the boat of it being an opportunity. We\u2019ve been preparing to expand our brand, the SuperBook, in other jurisdictions. How that will work will depend on the states and the specific regulations that will be set up.\u201d PASPA basically barred states from being able to legally accept wagers on sporting events; four states that had existing sports betting laws\u2014Nevada, Oregon, Delaware and Montana\u2014were grandfathered in and allowed to continue their programs. (Ironically, PASPA\u2019s main sponsor in the U.S. Senate was Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame forward Bill Bradley, who authored the bill while serving as Senator from New Jersey.) And, on the surface, who would have a problem with that? Which is the problem with surface-based analyses. What we don\u2019t know about the potential impacts of the SCOTUS decision is what\u2019s unnerving\u2014for professional sports leagues including the NBA, but, potentially, for so many other people connected either directly or tangentially with sports at all levels. There will certainly be unintended consequences of bringing gambling out into the open, with an impact that can\u2019t possibly be imagined or prepared for at this juncture. You simply cannot introduce this much money into the system of sports this quickly\u2014the sports betting industry in the United States, mostly in the shadows outside of the legal betting allowed in Nevada, is estimated to go through hundreds of millions of dollars annually\u2014without the river of dollars cutting through places with which it shouldn\u2019t connect. \u201cThere are so many parts to this,\u201d said Marc Ganis, the co-founder of SportsCorp, Ltd., a sports consulting firm that has assisted in the sale of NFL, NBA and Major League Baseball teams and the building of arenas and stadiums around the country for much of the last two decades, connecting prospective and current team owners to the leagues and to revenue sources that aid in the purchase of those teams and the building of their owners\u2019 new palaces. \u201cMany important parts are being, if not ignored, treated way too casually,\u201d Ganis said. \u201cIt\u2019s an important decision and will result in meaningful changes\u2014and not all of them will be positive.\u201d Chief among the many new concerns is, obviously, the threat of gambling and gamblers reaching teams and players\u2014or, even more worrisome, the mere accusation of untoward behaviors by team employees. We all know the tinfoil crowd is already out there, especially this time of year, when some claim every playoff game is fixed, either through result or point spread, to benefit some shady entity. \u201cAs the executive director of the players association, I\u2019m supposed to be seeing this as how to monetize this for the benefit of the players,\u201d Roberts said. \u201cBut there are so many other things that we have to anticipate addressing.\u201d The union anticipated a SCOTUS ruling that would allow gambling going forward when it negotiated the most recent Collective Bargaining Agreement with the NBA\u2014and provide the players with a potential cut of the new revenues generated. Article VII, Section 1, (a) (1) (xiii) states players will receive their share of Basketball Related Income including: All proceeds, net of Taxes, less reasonable and customary expenses (which expenses shall be subject to New Venture treatment, if applicable, under Section 1(a)(6)(iii) below), subject to the provisions of Section 1(a)(6) below, from gambling on NBA games or any aspect of NBA games, subject to appropriate treatment of categories of excluded revenues or other amounts, if applicable, under Section 1(a)(2) below and allocations for multi-element deals. BRI shall exclude revenues from gambling on NBA games or any aspect of NBA games generated by casinos or other gambling businesses, owned or operated by a Team, Related Party, or a League-related entity, whose total revenues are not predominantly from gambling on NBA games or any aspect of NBA games\u2026 Yet how can leagues adequately prepare for not just the influx of money, but the enhanced scrutiny that will follow every moment of every game going forward? Again: we\u2019re not even talking about the potential incentives to actually play cute with point spreads and\/or results of games. Point shaving scandals have roiled college basketball throughout the decades, from CCNY and Kentucky in the 1950s, to Boston College in the 1970s, to Arizona State to Tulane and Northwestern in the 1990s. Soccer, which is bet on legally around the world, hasn\u2019t fared all that well lately when it comes to keeping its sport out of the world spotlight for the wrong reasons. Ditto sports like cricket . Just the appearance and\/or accusation of same in our social media world today could be devastating; witness the corrosive effect of the claims of former NBA referee Tim Donaghy that NBA officials had been compromised. At base, scrutiny of players, coaches and other team officials could well increase to a level we have yet to see. \u201cAre the unions and the players prepared for some privacy invasions, similar to what takes place to testing for performance enhancing drugs, but now related to integrity\u2014which is a much less tangible matter?,\u201d Ganis asked. When you add up players, coaches and training staffs\u2014who would have the kind of access on player injuries that could be enticing to those who are putting down bets\u2014there could be up to \u201c600 people right off the bat who have to be monitored on a regular basis,\u201d Ganis said. \u201cAnd they\u2019re going to have to agree to this. The Players\u2019 Association had to agree that their members had to have their blood drawn or to give urine samples to test for drugs. What about if you want to look at their e-mails or their bank accounts?\u201d For that matter, he asks, what about garbage time, after which the result of the game has long been decided. A player who drives to the hole to score what would normally be a meaningless layup at the buzzer could impact the spread\u2014and would immediately fall under intense scrutiny. Roberts sees an even bigger adjustment that will have to be made. \u201cI have no issue or any reason to believe players will need to or need to change their in-game conduct,\u201d she said. \u201cI think our guys love this game. I don\u2019t have any worry that this is going to make players suddenly become cheaters. What I do worry about is the guy who says \u2018 I feel a little sore today,\u2019 and he really does, and someone saying to him from your environment that he\u2019s trying to affect the betting environment. \u201cYour (media) colleagues are going to have to be managed in terms of what kinds of questions are appropriate. You have people now asking Steph (Curry), \u2018are you sure your knee is okay?,\u2019 and him saying \u2018yes!\u2019 And I love that brother. In the new environment, you can imagine people accusing him of being disingenuous in terms of his health so that he can manipulate the spread. It could be really ugly.\u201d Nonetheless, the ruling was hailed by many who have skin in the game. Some who\u2019ve been on the front lines of the NBA\/gambling debate during the last few years don\u2019t believe there will be deleterious effects created by the SCOTUS ruling. They are not worried about potential integrity issues, feeling there could actually be enhancements created by new technology solutions. They understand we\u2019ve crossed the Rubicon as a country when it comes to gambling and understand the desire to move illegal wagering to legal betting, deprive organized crime of the profits and enhance state finances. Emerging companies like Swiss-based Sportradar, with which the NBA and the other major sports leagues in the United States have partnerships , produce and analyze enormous amounts of data about sporting events, which are provided to the various leagues, while also policing potential betting anomalies that could unearth shenanigans with point spreads and the like. The advent of daily fantasy sports betting, accelerated in 2006 after passage of the Unlawful Internet Gambling Enforcement Act (UIGEA), brought daily fantasy sports betting into the sunlight, with DraftKings and FanDuel, leaving no rational philosophical distinction between that and other forms of gambling. \u201cMany ask if this decision will impact the integrity of sports themselves. I think it\u2019s just the opposite,\u201d Washington Wizards owner Ted Leonsis said in a statement last week after the ruling was announced. \u201cI think that the increased transparency that will accompany more legalized betting around the country will only further protect against potential corruption. They say sunlight is the best disinfectant, and in this case I believe that is certainly true. \u201cOf course, there are a huge number of questions about how today\u2019s decision will play out across different states and throughout the different leagues. I don\u2019t claim to know all of those answers today, but what I do know is that this is a new frontier for professional sports and teams who don\u2019t seize on this opportunity will be left behind. As millennials and Gen Z continue to embrace the second screen, it\u2019s not hard to imagine in the near future fans on their devices analyzing data, placing bets and communicating with each other in real time during games. Legalized sports betting will only bring fans closer to the game, ramping up the action in each minute and creating more intensity. It will bring new revenue into the economy, creating jobs and growing our tax base. Today\u2019s decision is a great one for sports fans and I am eager to embrace it.\u201d In doing so, Leonsis echoes the position of NBA Commissioner Adam Silver, who wrote an op-ed in The New York Times in 2014 advocating the legalization of sports betting. It was a reversal of the league\u2019s previous position, which had been advocated for strongly by then-commissioner David Stern. Silver advocated passing federal laws that would allow states to accept legal wagers, but with uniform regulations and technological safeguards. (The league reiterated this position after the SCOTUS ruling last week.) \u201cLet me be clear: Any new approach must ensure the integrity of the game,\u201d Silver wrote back in 2014. \u201cOne of my most important responsibilities as commissioner of the NBA is to protect the integrity of professional basketball and preserve public confidence in the league and our sport. I oppose any course of action that would compromise these objectives. \u201cBut I believe that sports betting should be brought out of the underground and into the sunlight where it can be appropriately monitored and regulated.\u201d Along those lines, the NBA and other sports leagues are already advocating for a cut of the new potential revenues, arguing that they not only provide the apparatus and platforms for games, but will have to make additional investments to investigate potential suspicious activities. The so-called \u201cintegrity fee\u201d argued for by the leagues could be up to one percent of all monies bet on games. \u201cThe issue of the integrity fee is a really good one,\u201d Ganis said. \u201cDo I think the leagues should receive a fee? The answer is unequivocally yes. The reason for it is simple\u2014they are the ones putting on the events that are being gambled on. It\u2019s like a casino that has a poker tournament. They take a cut of every pot, because they\u2019re hosting it. They bring in the dealers, they provide the venues, they make sure no one\u2019s cheating\u2026they take the same cut of the tournament that the leagues are asking for.\u201d Roberts concurs. \u201cThe league shares, we share the same interest in maintaining the integrity of the game,\u201d she said. \u201cThere\u2019s more common space there\u2014no difference in terms of our interests\u2026we do share with the league the notion that it\u2019s somewhat unseemly that people are going to make billions of dollars on a product that we\u2019ve created. We fight about enough. It\u2019s sort of refreshing that we can find, without any real difference between us, something that we can try to resolve together.\u201d Of course, the gaming industry demurs. \u201cWe\u2019ve been doing that for 40 years,\u201d Kornegay said. \u201cThis is nothing new to us. We\u2019ve been protecting the games and the product for four decades. Some have been acting like we haven\u2019t been doing this. I met with the leagues 14 years ago in Indianapolis and we told them, at the time, we were on the same side. We want to protect the game like you do. Integrity is the name of the game for us.\u201d Casinos have entire departments who monitor spreads and that are the first to blow the whistle when something doesn\u2019t quite smell right or add up with a spread. \u201cIt\u2019s not periodically or a spot check,\u201d Kornegay said. \u201cThey check everything we do\u2014on our side of the counter and on the other side of the counter. When they talk about the integrity fee, I\u2019ve heard some say if there\u2019s a scandal, the leagues are going to take a hit. Well, we\u2019re going to take a hit too\u2026people aren\u2019t going to want to bet on something that they don\u2019t think is fair and true.\u201d In addition, states such as Nevada already assess significant taxes on casinos and other gambling establishments\u2014in Nevada\u2019s case, a graduated tax rate that tops out at 6.75 percent\u2014that make profit margins smaller. Now, no one\u2019s planning a telethon for the owners of Mandalay Bay or the Bellagio. But an integrity fee would cut into their net. \u201cSports books are amenities to their casinos, not a revenue generator,\u201d Kornegay said. \u201c\u2026.we\u2019re not shoveling out gold every day. It\u2019s a very volatile game. It\u2019s the only casino game that doesn\u2019t have a mathematical probability (favoring the house) in it. We lose a lot.\u201d (The NHL expansion Vegas Golden Knights, which advanced to the Stanley Cup finals Sunday with a Western Conference finals win over Winnipeg, stand to provide a rare but nonetheless bracing financial hit to sports books like Kornegay\u2019s.) We are just at the beginning of this, of course, and there\u2019s no guarantee that legalizing betting is going to slay the economic golden goose. There could well be unintended positives, too. (Bookmakers, for example, are going to have to market their services on a larger scale , which could produce larger revenue streams for leagues and their teams.) After all: the only thing left in Pandora\u2019s jar\/box after she opened it was hope. \u201cAdam is, arguably, the smartest person I\u2019ve ever met,\u201d Ganis said. \u201cAdam Silver is brilliant. He\u2019ll figure this out. But it needs to be figured out.\u201d *** Longtime NBA reporter, columnist and Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Famer David Aldridge is an analyst for TNT. The views on this page do not necessarily reflect the views of the NBA, its clubs or Turner Broadcasting."},{"id":40422,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/morning-tip-pre-combine-interviews-bring-interesting-tidbits","date":"2018-05-21","title":"Pre-combine interviews bring interesting tidbits","content":"Last week, a team interviewing West Virginia guard Jevon Carter at the Chicago pre-Draft combine had what seemed an innocuous question for the hard-nosed point guard: you gonna be ready to play every game, every night, 82 nights a season. \u201cYeah,\u201d Carter said, defiantly. \u201cThat\u2019s what I do.\u201d The combine is certainly for measuring the heights and weights and wingspans of players likely to be taken in next month\u2019s Draft \u2014such as Texas freshman big Mo Bamba\u2019s insane 7-10 wingspan , which will do nothing to harm his Lottery prospects. It is certainly for seeing the guys who do deign to play against one another compete, and potentially change some minds, such as last year, when the University of Utah\u2019s Kyle Kuzma shot the ball from deep better than he had in three seasons with the Utes and became a definite first-round possibility. But the Combine is also for the interviews\u2014each team can interview up to 18 players. Teams interview players in different ranges, from those they\u2019re very interested in taking in the first round to those who likely would just be training camp and\/or summer league team invitees. Last week provided some impressive interactions between players and teams, and a lot of funny ones, as happens every year. So we asked a bunch of teams to share some of the best answers they got from players during the interviews, to provide a sense of who at least gave some thought to what they wanted to say beforehand, and who displayed an acuity to think on their feet. Among those who came across as the best interviews, per league sources, were Bamba (\u201chands down,\u201d one source said), Alabama guard Collin Sexton (\u201cedge and confidence came through in his interview,\u201d another team\u2019s official said, Duke\u2019s Wendell Carter, Maryland forward Bruno Fernando (\u201cimpressive,\u201d per another source), Tulane\u2019s Melvin Frazier (\u201cvery honest,\u201d one team official said) and Missouri forward Michael Porter, Jr. Then, there were the more light-hearted exchanges. One player quizzed his prospective team, going down the line asking \u201cwho are you guys? And describe what you do for your organization?\u201d \u201cFirst time I\u2019ve heard that question from a player in 25 years,\u201d a longtime team executive said. The Suns, according to a source, interviewed a player who is a projected top five pick\u2014which made sense, considering Phoenix has the top pick in the Draft after winning the Lottery. The player told the assembled front office and coaches, \u201dI\u2019d love to play for the Phoenix Suns. I\u2019m not just saying that because you guys have the number one pick\u2014I really feel like I\u2019m the best player in the Draft and the best fit for your roster. I\u2019d be saying that even if you guys didn\u2019t have the number one pick. I don\u2019t care where I get picked\u2014I just want to be in Phoenix.\u201d It was impressive. After a beat, Suns GM Ryan McDonough answered: \u2018Great. We also have the 16th pick. Do you want to try to work something out so we can pick you at 16?\u2019 Player: Silence. Followed by the room breaking up. Another player, likely to go in the top half of the first round, told a team that he played to about 90 percent of his potential each night in college.
