The views on this page do not necessarily reflect the views of the NBA, its clubs or Turner Broadcasting."},{"id":40527,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/boston-celtics-brad-stevens-remains-humble-team-continues-thrive","date":"2018-05-12","title":"Boston Celtics' Brad Stevens remains humble as team continues to thrive","content":" WALTHAM, Mass. \u2014 When Brad Stevens accepted the Celtics head coaching job five years ago, he didn\u2019t allow himself to get caught up in thinking about how he could add his name to the franchise\u2019s rich history. He was too busy trying to figure out how to avoid being buried under it. \u201dYou realize that if you\u2019re going to break records here, you\u2019re probably going to break bad ones,\u201d he recently said. \u201dBecause none of the good ones are reachable.\u201d While achieving Red Auerbach status may not be on Stevens\u2019 radar, in just his fifth season there\u2019s no question the 41-year-old is also beyond being the wide-eyed former Butler University coach who arrived in Boston. In a timeframe that has often already swallowed up most first-time NBA coaches, he\u2019s managed to endear himself to a championship-driven city by helping Boston make an improbable run back to the Eastern Conference finals. The Celtics seemingly had their championship hopes derailed following the season-ending injuries to both of their offseason additions in Gordon Hayward and Kyrie Irving. Yet, Boston won 55 games during the regular season and increased its win total for the fifth consecutive season under Stevens. Despite having a roster that was down to just 11 healthy players by the end of their second-round win over Philadelphia , the Celtics enter their conference finals rematch with Cleveland on Sunday with an 8-0 record at home this postseason. They are also the first team in NBA history to make it back to this point without their leading scorer from the regular season (Irving). Most of the NBA community was taken aback after Stevens failed to receive a single vote from his peers when the National Basketball Coaches Association gave out its coach of the year award . The honor went to Toronto\u2019s Dwane Casey, who was fired Friday after his team was swept in the East semifinals by the Cleveland Cavaliers . Stevens has always downplayed the attention placed on coaching awards. He said that he thought Casey deserved the honor and didn\u2019t expect him to be without a job for long. Boston\u2019s successes this season aside, Stevens said comfort remains a commodity this profession. \u201dI don\u2019t think that I would ever define anybody in the coaching or playing shoes probably as comfortable,\u201d he said. \u201dYou\u2019re just focused on what\u2019s next. But it is basketball. There\u2019s only so much you can do.\u201d But it\u2019s also clear that one of the reasons that Casey lost his job was the Raptors\u2019 inability to challenge the Cavs in the postseason. Toronto was also swept out of the playoffs by Cleveland last season. Most of the credit for Boston\u2019s run thus far surely belongs to veteran Al Horford and the Celtics\u2019 corps of young players, including Terry Rozier, Jaylen Brown and rookie Jayson Tatum. Stevens agrees with that assessment and has remained true to his style by blending into the background in public, instead waiting for the huddle or practice to make his voice heard. He believes his team\u2019s mental toughness and grit have carried it more than anything he\u2019s done. Horford said Stevens hasn\u2019t shied away from putting their young players in pressure situations. \u201dI think a lot of our guys have been thrown into the fire. I think it\u2019s been designed that way so guys can just develop and learn as they go,\u201d Horford said. \u201dBut I think that one of the things that helps them is the way that coach helps them prepare and the way that he teaches them the game.\u201d There is also at least one person watching from afar who thinks a lot of the credit belongs to Stevens. And it just happens to be the same player he will spend the next few weeks trying to stop: LeBron James. From Stevens\u2019 ability to draw up plays out of timeouts, to his management of late-clock situations, to getting the best out of his roster, James has long been a fan. \u201dI think they are one of the most well-coached teams in our league,\u201d James said. \u201dNo matter who has played for them, he can put guys in position to succeed and get the most out of whoever has been in their lineup over the past few years. It\u2019s not just this year.\u201d Stevens said he\u2019s focused on living in the moment. \u201dFrom our standpoint, I feel like it\u2019s been a lot of fun,\u201d he said. \u201dWe talked about it prior to the playoffs; nobody should love a challenge more, nobody should have more fun doing it. I think our guys have done a good job with that.\u201d And though he may never say it, so has their coach. \u2014 AP Sports Writer Tom Withers in Independence, Ohio contributed to this report."}]
